       26  
       27  ## Architecture: Producer → Gate → Next Producer
       28  
       27 -Each agent node produces output, then a deterministic gate val
          -idator checks it (zero LLM cost). If the gate fails, the produ
          -cer retries with error context injected into state. After `max
          -_gate_retries` (default 2), the pipeline proceeds anyway.     
       29 +Core pattern from `graph.py`: each agent node produces output,
          + then a deterministic gate validator checks it (zero LLM cost)
          +. If the gate fails, the producer retries with error context i
          +njected into `step_validation` state field. After `max_gate_re
          +tries` (default 2), the pipeline proceeds anyway to avoid infi
          +nite loops.                                                   
       30  
       29 -### Pipeline Flow (from `graph.py`)                           
       31 +### Pipeline Flow                                             
       32  
       33  ```
       34  START → orchestrator → gate_orchestrator
       33 -  → fan_out_parsers → [datastage_parser, sql_interpreter, ddl_
          -parser] (PARALLEL)                                            
       35 +  → fan_out_parsers → [datastage_parser, sql_interpreter, ddl_
          +parser] (PARALLEL, 2 at a time)                               
       36    → gate_parsers → pattern_mapper → gate_mapper
       35 -  → spark_sql_generator → gate_sql → config_generator → gate_c
          -onfig                                                         
       37 +  → spark_sql_generator → gate_sql (deterministic + LLM busine
          +ss logic check)                                               
       38 +  → config_generator → gate_config (deterministic + LLM cross-
          +reference check)                                              
       39    → schema_validator → human_approval → END
       40  ```
       41  
       39 -### Gate Routing Logic                                        
       42 +**Key routing logic:**                                        
       43 +- `gate_sql` and `gate_config`: run deterministic checks first
          +, then LLM checks ONLY if deterministic passed (saves tokens).
          + Controlled by `gate_llm_checks` config flag (can disable for 
          +faster demos).                                                
       44 +- `schema_validator`: score >= 0.80 → human_approval; score < 
          +0.80 → retry once then human_approval regardless.             
       45 +- `human_approval`: approved → END; rejected → back to `spark_
          +sql_generator`.                                               
       46 +- `fan_out_parsers`: no-op passthrough node needed because Lan
          +gGraph conditional edges can't fan out directly.              
       47  
       41 -Every gate follows the same pattern (`_route_gate`):          
       42 -- **Passed** → next node                                      
       43 -- **Failed + retries < MAX_GATE_RETRIES** → retry the producer
       44 -- **Failed + retries >= MAX_GATE_RETRIES** → proceed anyway (d
          -on't loop forever)                                            
       48 +### Concurrency and Retry                                     
       49  
       46 -Special cases:                                                
       47 -- `gate_sql` and `gate_config` run deterministic checks first,
          - then LLM checks only if deterministic passed (saves tokens)  
       48 -- `schema_validator` routes: score >= 0.80 → human_approval, s
          -core < 0.80 → retry once then human_approval                  
       49 -- `human_approval` routes: approved → END, rejected → back to 
          -spark_sql_generator                                           
       50 +From `pipeline_config.yaml`:                                  
       51 +- `graph_max_concurrency`: 8 (max parallel nodes in a superste
          +p)                                                            
       52 +- `ddl_parser_batch`: 8, `sql_interpreter_batch`: 8, `config_g
          +enerator_batch`: 6 (parallel LLM calls within an agent)       
       53 +- `max_gate_retries`: 2 per gate before force-proceeding      
       54 +- `llm_max_attempts`: 5 with exponential backoff (2s initial, 
          +2x factor, 60s max) for Azure 529 errors                      
       55 +- `per_stage_retries`: 3 (max retries per SQL generation stage
          +)                                                             
       56  
       51 -### Model Assignments                                         
       57 +**Orchestrator mode:** `pipeline.orchestrator_mode` can be `"r
          +eact"` (full ReAct agent with tools, needed for MCP) or `"dire
          +ct"` (Python calls tools directly, single LLM call for pipelin
          +e ID, faster for demos).                                      
       58  
       53 -| Model | Agents |                                            
       54 -|-------|--------|                                            
       55 -| **Opus** | datastage_parser, pattern_mapper, spark_sql_gener
          -ator (plan + dependent phases) |                              
       56 -| **Sonnet** | orchestrator, sql_interpreter, ddl_parser, spar
          -k_sql_generator (independent phase), config_generator, schema_
          -validator |

       61 +## State Schema (`state.py`: `ETLMigrationState`)             
       62 +                                                              
       63 +TypedDict with custom reducers:                               
       64 +                                                              
       65 +| Field | Type | Reducer | Purpose |                          
       66 +|-------|------|---------|---------|                          
       67 +| `messages` | list[AnyMessage] | add_messages (append+dedup) 
          +| LangGraph message history |                                 
       68 +| `source_artifacts` | list[dict] | last-write | [{type, name,
          + content}] input files |                                      
       69 +| `target_examples` | list[dict] | last-write | [{type, name, 
          +content}] reference outputs |                                 
       70 +| `source_schemas` | dict | last-write | {table: {columns: [{n
          +ame, type, nullable}]}} |                                     
       71 +| `datastage_parsed` | dict | last-write | Structured XML pars
          +e with embedded_sql, stages, tables, columns, llm_analysis |  
       72 +| `sql_interpreted` | list[dict] | last-write | Business rules
          + from stored procedures (per-artifact) |                      
       73 +| `ddl_schemas` | list[dict] | last-write | Parsed DDL/view sc
          +hemas with parsed_schemas per file |                          
       74 +| `pattern_mapping` | dict | last-write | Legacy→Databricks ma
          +pping rules (llm_analysis field) |                            
       75 +| `spark_sql_output` | str | last-write | Generated Spark SQL 
          +(all CREATE TEMP VIEW statements) |                           
       76 +| `yaml_config` | str | last-write | Pipeline YAML |          
       77 +| `deployment_yaml` | str | last-write | Deployment YAML |    
       78 +| `hql_ddl` | str | last-write | CREATE TABLE HQL |           
       79 +| `validation_result` | dict | last-write | {status, overall_s
          +core, issues[], sections[]} |                                 
       80 +| `_gate_llm_checks` | list[dict] | operator.add (accumulate) 
          +| LLM findings from gate_sql + gate_config |                  
       81 +| `step_validation` | dict | last-write | Gate feedback for re
          +trying agents: {node, passed, checks[], errors[], warnings[]} 
          +|                                                             
       82 +| `current_stage` | str | _last_stage (handles parallel writes
          +) | Current pipeline position |                               
       83 +| `retry_count` | int | last-write | Gate retry counter |     
       84 +| `run_id` | str | last-write | Unique run identifier |       
       85 +| `input_hash` | str | last-write | SHA-256 of all input artif
          +acts |                                                        
       86 +| `approval_count` | int | last-write | Consecutive approval c
          +ount |                                                        
       87 +| `auto_approve_threshold` | int | last-write | Skip review af
          +ter N approvals |                                             
       88 +                                                              
       89 +Custom `_last_stage` reducer: when parallel parsers all write 
          +to `current_stage` simultaneously, LangGraph passes a list. Th
          +e reducer picks the last value.                               
       90 +

       97 +| Agent | Model | Rationale |                                 
       98 +|-------|-------|-----------|                                 
       99 +| orchestrator | Sonnet | Fast routing, no heavy reasoning nee
          +ded |                                                         
      100 +| datastage_parser | **Opus** | Complex XML analysis with 1M c
          +ontext |                                                      
      101 +| sql_interpreter | Sonnet | SQL structure extraction, batch p
          +arallel |                                                     
      102 +| ddl_parser | Sonnet | Schema extraction, batch parallel |   
      103 +| pattern_mapper | **Opus** | Critical mapping step, needs ful
          +l context |                                                   
      104 +| spark_sql_generator (plan) | **Opus** | Plans all stages and
          + dependency graph |                                           
      105 +| spark_sql_generator (independent) | Sonnet | Generates indep
          +endent stages (simpler) |                                     
      106 +| spark_sql_generator (dependent) | **Opus** | Generates depen
          +dent stages (needs full context) |                            
      107 +| config_generator | Sonnet | Template-based, 3 parallel calls
          + |                                                            
      108 +| schema_validator | Sonnet | Cross-checks, no generation |

       86 -Key design: `current_stage` uses a custom `_last_stage` reduce
          -r to handle concurrent writes from parallel parser nodes.     
      110 +---                                                           
      111  
      112 +## Agents (10 files in `agents/`)                             
      113 +                                                              
      114 +### orchestrator.py                                           
      115 +- Two modes: `react` (full ReAct agent with tools for MCP/blob
          +) and `direct` (Python calls `load_all_artifacts` directly, si
          +ngle LLM call for pipeline ID). Direct mode is faster for demo
          +s.                                                            
      116 +- Loads files from `docs/ETL_use_case/` (local) or Azure Blob 
          +Storage (production).                                         
      117 +- Classifies artifacts by content (DataStage XML, stored proce
          +dure, DDL, view, schema, Scala app, YAML, HQL).               
      118 +- **Side-channel pattern:** file content stored in `_artifact_
          +store` dict, NOT returned to LLM. LLM only sees metadata (name
          +, type, size). Prevents 1.3M char XML from consuming context. 
      119 +- Filters targets by pipeline name matching (e.g., `inventory_
          +periodic_daily`).                                             
      120 +- Generates `run_id` and `input_hash` for reproducibility.    
      121 +                                                              
      122 +### datastage_parser.py                                       
      123 +- **NOT a ReAct agent.** Deterministic extraction + single LLM
          + synthesis.                                                   
      124 +- Step 1 (Python, zero tokens): `extract_job_metadata`, `extra
          +ct_embedded_sql`, `extract_column_definitions` from XML.      
      125 +- Step 2 (1 Opus call): synthesize findings into structured an
          +alysis.                                                       
      126 +- Uses `sqlglot` (T-SQL dialect) to extract table names from e
          +mbedded SQL fragments.                                        
      127 +- Cross-references LLM-mentioned tables against deterministic 
          +extraction.                                                   
      128 +- Quick parse mode for XMLs > 200K chars (skips LLM, determini
          +stic only).                                                   
      129 +                                                              
      130 +### sql_interpreter.py                                        
      131 +- Sonnet model, batch parallel processing.                    
      132 +- Step 1 (Python): `sqlglot` extracts tables, joins, CTEs, tem
          +p tables from T-SQL stored procedures and views.              
      133 +- Step 2 (Parallel LLM): `llm.batch()` processes all SP/view a
          +rtifacts in parallel (batch size from config).                
      134 +- Cleans T-SQL artifacts (GO, USE, SET) before parsing.       
      135 +                                                              
      136 +### ddl_parser.py                                             
      137 +- Same pattern as sql_interpreter: sqlglot extraction + parall
          +el LLM batch.                                                 
      138 +- Extracts table names, column names with FULL precision (e.g.
          +, `decimal(13,3)`), nullable constraints, primary keys.       
      139 +- Handles both CREATE TABLE and CREATE VIEW statements.       
      140 +                                                              
      141 +### pattern_mapper.py                                         
      142 +- **Single Opus call.** Reads all parser outputs + target exam
          +ples.                                                         
      143 +- Produces translation dictionary: surrogate keys → business k
          +eys, SQL Server types → Databricks types, temp tables → interm
          +ediate views, CASE WHEN → withColumn patterns, etc.           
      144 +- Builds context from deterministic fields first, falls back t
          +o LLM analysis.                                               
      145 +                                                              
      146 +### spark_sql_generator.py                                    
      147 +- Three-phase generation (the proven 0.97-scoring approach):  
      148 +  1. **Plan** (1 Opus call): Analyzes full Scala app, extracts
          + stage snippets, builds dependency graph (independent vs depen
          +dent stages).                                                 
      149 +  2. **Phase 1** (1 Sonnet call): Generates all independent st
          +ages.                                                         
      150 +  3. **Phase 2** (1 Opus call): Generates dependent stages wit
          +h Phase 1 output as context.                                  
      151 +- On **retry**: passes previous SQL + gate errors to Opus for 
          +targeted fix (1 call, not 3).                                 
      152 +- Deduplicates views (last occurrence wins).                  
      153 +- Context limits from config prevent prompt overflow.         
      154 +                                                              
      155 +### config_generator.py                                       
      156 +- **3 parallel Sonnet calls** via `llm.batch()`: pipeline YAML
          +, deployment YAML, create.HQL.                                
      157 +- Each call gets the target template as ground truth and is to
          +ld to copy structure exactly, only changing values where neede
          +d.                                                            
      158 +- Shared context: pattern mapping + source schemas + generated
          + Spark SQL.                                                   
      159 +                                                              
      160 +### schema_validator.py                                       
      161 +- **Zero LLM calls.** Deterministic cross-checks + assembly of
          + upstream gate LLM results.                                   
      162 +- Organizes checks into 4 sections for dashboard rendering: Sp
          +ark SQL, HQL DDL, Pipeline YAML, Deployment Config.           
      163 +- Computes overall_score by combining deterministic pass rates
          + with LLM findings (warnings deduct 0.2, bugs deduct more).   
      164 +- Produces the `validation_result` dict that the review screen
          + displays.                                                    
      165 +                                                              
      166 +### review_agent.py (AI Review)                               
      167 +- Tool-using agent for surgical SQL review and fix.           
      168 +- Tools: `read_sql`, `read_scala`, `read_validation`, `patch_v
          +iew` (surgically replace a specific view's SQL), `run_validati
          +on` (re-run checks on current SQL).                           
      169 +- Single conversation thread (not split into review + fix like
          + before).                                                     
      170 +- Module-level `_review_context` dict set by API server before
          + each conversation.                                           
      171 +                                                              
      172 +### human_approval.py                                         
      173 +- Uses LangGraph `interrupt()` for human-in-the-loop.         
      174 +- Auto-approves after threshold reached (configurable, default
          + 1 for demo = always manual).                                 
      175 +- Approved → increment counter, proceed to END.               
      176 +- Rejected → reset counter, add error, route back to `spark_sq
          +l_generator`.                                                 
      177 +                                                              
      178  ---

       90 -## Agents (in `src/etl_agent/agents/`)                        
      180 +## Validators (`validators.py` — 900+ lines)                  
      181  
       92 -| Agent | File | Purpose |                                    
       93 -|-------|------|---------|                                    
       94 -| Orchestrator | `orchestrator.py` | Loads source files, class
          -ifies artifacts, selects pipeline |                           
       95 -| DataStage Parser | `datastage_parser.py` | Parses DataStage 
          -XML: job stages, transformations, source/target connections, d
          -ata flow. Deterministic + LLM. |                              
       96 -| SQL Interpreter | `sql_interpreter.py` | Analyzes stored pro
          -cedures: table joins, CTEs, temp tables, business logic, aggre
          -gation patterns. SQLGlot + LLM. |                             
       97 -| DDL Parser | `ddl_parser.py` | Parses DDL files and views: t
          -able/column names, data types, constraints, precisions. SQLGlo
          -t + LLM. |                                                    
       98 -| Pattern Mapper | `pattern_mapper.py` | Creates SQL-to-Spark 
          -translation dictionary using target examples. Single Opus call
          -. |                                                           
       99 -| Spark SQL Generator | `spark_sql_generator.py` | Three-step:
          - plan stages → dependency graph → generate independent then de
          -pendent stages. Also has v2 version. |                        
      100 -| Config Generator | `config_generator.py` | Generates 3 files
          - in parallel: pipeline YAML, deployment YAML, create.HQL |    
      101 -| Schema Validator | `schema_validator.py` | Final cross-artif
          -act validation, produces score and issues |                   
      102 -| Review Agent | `review_agent.py` | AI review/audit of valida
          -tion results (the "AI Review" button) |                       
      103 -| Human Approval | `human_approval.py` | Approval gate with au
          -to-approve threshold |                                        
      182 +All deterministic (zero LLM cost) with source grounding checks
          +.                                                             
      183  
      184 +### Core patterns:                                            
      185 +- **Source grounding:** builds lowercase corpus from all sourc
          +e/target artifacts, checks if generated names actually exist i
          +n original files. Prevents hallucination.                     
      186 +- **sqlglot:** AST-based table and column extraction from both
          + T-SQL and Spark SQL dialects.                                
      187 +- **YAML validation:** custom safe loader that handles Databri
          +cks `!secret` tags.                                           
      188 +                                                              
      189 +### validate_orchestrator                                     
      190 +- Checks: source artifacts loaded, has DataStage XML, has targ
          +et examples, all artifacts have content, run_id set.          
      191 +                                                              
      192 +### validate_parsers                                          
      193 +- DataStage: has stages, has embedded SQL, has tables (sqlglot
          +), has columns, has LLM analysis (>100 chars).                
      194 +- Cross-check: compare deterministic tables vs LLM-mentioned t
          +ables. Warns on discrepancies.                                
      195 +- SQL interpreter: present check. DDL: present + column names 
          +grounded in source.                                           
      196 +                                                              
      197 +### validate_pattern_mapper                                   
      198 +- Mapping non-empty, mentions actual source table names from D
          +DL schemas.                                                   
      199 +- Checks for key concepts: source references, type mappings, c
          +olumn mappings.                                               
      200 +                                                              
      201 +### validate_spark_sql (most complex, ~230 lines)             
      202 +- SQL not empty and substantial (>5000 chars, real migration i
          +s 10K+).                                                      
      203 +- **sqlglot syntax check:** parse statement by statement, pass
          + rate >= 50%.                                                 
      204 +- **DDL table coverage:** at least 30% of DDL tables must appe
          +ar in SQL.                                                    
      205 +- **Column coverage:** at least 20% of known DDL columns in SQ
          +L.                                                            
      206 +- **Source table grounding:** FROM/JOIN table refs checked aga
          +inst source+target corpus. Excludes intermediate views the SQL
          + itself creates. Warns on ungrounded names.                   
      207 +- **Truncation detection:** both end-of-file and per-view. Che
          +cks if SQL ends with comma/AND/OR/ON/=. Checks each CREATE TEM
          +P VIEW for missing semicolons.                                
      208 +- **HQL column match:** if HQL DDL exists, its columns should 
          +appear in SQL.                                                
      209 +                                                              
      210 +### validate_config_generator                                 
      211 +- Pipeline YAML: non-empty (>200 chars), valid YAML structure.
      212 +- Deployment YAML: non-empty (>100 chars), valid YAML.        
      213 +- HQL: has CREATE TABLE statement.                            
      214 +- **Source grounding:** HQL column names must exist in target 
          +corpus. YAML sourceFile names must exist in source corpus.    
      215 +                                                              
      216 +### LLM gate checks (llm_check_sql, llm_check_config)         
      217 +- Run AFTER deterministic checks pass. Called from `gate_sql` 
          +and `gate_config`.                                            
      218 +- `llm_check_sql`: extracts view dependency graph from SQL, se
          +nds to LLM with Scala target for business logic verification. 
          +Two checks: column_existence and business_logic_preservation. 
      219 +- Supports multi-turn: on retry, includes previous findings an
          +d AI Review verdicts so LLM doesn't re-flag resolved issues.  
      220 +- `llm_check_config`: verifies YAML token names, column type c
          +onsistency vs SQL CASTs, deployment config structure.         
      221 +

      226 +### artifact_tools.py

      228 +- `load_all_artifacts`: walks directories, classifies each fil

      229 +- Classification logic: checks content patterns (XML detection
          +, CREATE PROCEDURE, CREATE TABLE, YAML structure, Scala patter
          +ns).                                                          
      230 +- Two backends: local filesystem and Azure Blob Storage.

          -les present, run ID generated |

      232 +### xml_parser.py

      234 +- `extract_job_metadata`: job name, stage count, descriptions 
          +from DSExport format.                                         
      235 +- `extract_embedded_sql`: finds SQL in stage properties (custo

      240 +### sql_tools.py                                              
      241 +- `parse_sql_structure`: sqlglot-based extraction of tables, j
          +oins, CTEs, temp tables, statement types.                     
      242 +- Deterministic, no LLM needed for structure.                 
      243  
      244 +### datastage_tools.py                                        
      245 +- Side-channel store (`_ds_store`): XML content pre-loaded by 
          +parser node before agent starts.                              
      246 +- Tools: `get_job_overview`, `get_embedded_sql`, `get_column_d
          +efinitions`, `list_stages`, `read_stage`, `search_xml`, `write
          +_notes` (scratchpad).                                         
      247 +- LLM never sees raw XML; tools return summaries.             
      248 +                                                              
      249 +### scratchpad.py                                             
      250 +- Simple key-value note storage for agents to record findings

      251 +- `write_notes(key, content)` and `read_notes(key)`.          
      252 +- Cleared between agent runs.                                 
      253 +                                                              
      254 +### blob_storage.py

      257 +                                                              
      258 +### result.py

      263 +## Prompts (12 files in `prompts/`)                           
      264 +                                                              
      265 +Each prompt is a system message defining the agent's role, wor
          +kflow, and output rules.                                      
      266 +                                                              
      267 +| Prompt | Key Instructions |                                 
      268 +|--------|-----------------|                                  
      269 +| `orchestrator.txt` | Discover/load/classify artifacts, ident
          +ify pipeline name from target Scala apps |                    
      270 +| `datastage_parser.txt` | Tool-based XML exploration workflow
          + (5 steps), scratchpad usage for consistency |                
      271 +| `sql_interpreter.txt` | Extract business rules (flag calcula
          +tions, SKU_Behavior thresholds, dotcom handling, temp tables, 
          +7-day lookbacks) |                                            
      272 +| `ddl_parser.txt` | Extract COMPLETE schema with EXACT decima
          +l precision. Every column, every constraint. |                
      273 +| `pattern_mapper.txt` | Map 9+ legacy pattern types (surrogat
          +e keys, types, temp tables, EXISTS subqueries, CASE WHEN, GETD
          +ATE, NOLOCK hints, CAST, Scala helper functions) |            
      274 +| `spark_sql_planner.txt` | Output dependency graph: `Stage N 
          +(viewName) -- INDEPENDENT/DEPENDENT on Stages X,Y` |          
      275 +| `spark_sql_generator.txt` | Two-phase generation. Quality ru
          +les: exact type precision, no invented COALESCE, copy CASE/WHE
          +N mappings verbatim from Scala |                              
      276 +| `spark_sql_stage_generator.txt` | Single-stage generation. R
          +aw SQL only, no markdown, starts with CREATE OR REPLACE TEMP V
          +IEW, ends with semicolon |                                    
      277 +| `config_generator.txt` | Copy target templates EXACTLY. Do N
          +OT invent token names, add/remove columns, or modify deploymen
          +t settings |                                                  
      278 +| `schema_validator.txt` | 5 semantic checks (YAML structure, 
          +column types, column existence, business logic, deployment). F
          +ocus on what code can't judge. |                              
      279 +| `gate_sql_llm.txt` | 2 checks (column existence, business lo
          +gic). Two-phase analysis: first use scratchpad to think, then 
          +output JSON. Impact-aware scoring using dependency graph. |   
      280 +| `gate_config_llm.txt` | 3 checks (YAML structure, column typ
          +es, deployment). Match against target examples exactly. |

      202 -## Key Technical Details for Demo                             
      376 +## Key Design Patterns                                        
      377  
      204 -1. **Concurrency:** `max_concurrency=2` on compile (3 parallel
          - parsers run 2 at a time)                                     
      205 -2. **Retry policy:** Handles Azure 529 (Overloaded) with backo
          -ff                                                            
      206 -3. **Checkpointing:** PostgreSQL via `langgraph.checkpoint.pos
          -tgres.PostgresSaver`                                          
      207 -4. **LangSmith:** Connected for tracing (waterfall view of all
          - API calls)                                                   
      208 -5. **Run time:** ~9.5 minutes end-to-end per the CLAUDE.md    
      378 +1. **Side-channel stores:** File content stored in module-leve
          +l dicts, not in LLM context. Prevents massive files (1.3M char
          + XML) from consuming context windows. Both `_artifact_store` (
          +orchestrator) and `_ds_store` (DataStage tools) use this patte
          +rn.                                                           
      379 +                                                              
      380 +2. **Deterministic-first:** Every agent does Python/sqlglot ex
          +traction before LLM calls. LLM fills gaps and adds semantic un
          +derstanding. Gates are deterministic (zero LLM cost) by defaul
          +t, with optional LLM checks gated behind a config flag.       
      381 +                                                              
      382 +3. **Source grounding:** Validators build text corpora from or
          +iginal source files and check that generated names (tables, co
          +lumns, source files) actually exist. Catches hallucination bef
          +ore it propagates.                                            
      383 +                                                              
      384 +4. **Retry with feedback:** Gate errors are written to `step_v
          +alidation` in state. Agents read this field on entry to know e
          +xactly what to fix. Retry messages include the specific errors
          +. Max retries configurable per gate.                          
      385 +                                                              
      386 +5. **Parallel execution:** Three parsers run in parallel (fan-
          +out/fan-in). SQL generator plans first then generates independ
          +ent stages in parallel (max concurrency 4). Config generator r
          +uns 3 files in parallel. All via `llm.batch()` or LangGraph ed
          +ges.                                                          
      387 +                                                              
      388 +6. **Template-based config generation:** Config generator copi
          +es target templates exactly, only changing values where data r
          +equires. This ensures output matches Sephora's existing Aggreg
          +ationApplication framework format.                            
      389 +

● Makes perfect sense. The 30 hours breaks down cleanly:

  - Week 1 (8 hours): Discovery meetings, paced by Sephora's availability. Not
  full-time on your side. This is the part that depends on them.
  - Week 2 (20 hours): The actual mapping work, heads-down and autonomous. This
  is where the value is produced.
  - Buffer (2 hours): Follow-ups, edge cases.

  The key constraint is Week 1. If they can get SMEs available quickly, the
  whole thing moves fast. If scheduling is slow on their end, Week 1 stretches
  but your hours don't change. The 30-hour estimate holds either way.

  demo?

● Here is the picture, and it is more important than it first appeared.

  Maher Burhan is not just a random consultant. He works for Xebia, a Databricks
   Elite Partner that has a shipping product called the Agentic Data Pipeline 
  Migrator that does almost exactly what your demo does: multi-agent
  architecture, SQL and ETL codebase conversion, Databricks-ready output,
  auditable reports. It is listed on Databricks' own blog as a GenAI Partner
  Accelerator.

  The good news:
  - He has been collaborative since Set 04, not adversarial
  - He literally suggested the approach that made the demo possible
  (disconnected, use exported XML)
  - All other vendors were dismissed. If Xebia were competing, they would
  already be in the conversation as a vendor.
  - He is embedded as Sephora's architect, not selling Xebia's products

  The risk:
  - He knows what good looks like in this space because his employer builds the
  same thing
  - The bar just got higher. He will ask technically precise questions.
  - The unspoken comparison in his mind will be "could Xebia's product do this?"
   even if he never says it

  BayOne's differentiation against a generic migrator like Xebia's:
  1. Custom output format. BayOne produces Sephora's specific YAML configs for
  the AggregationApplication framework. A generic migrator produces Databricks
  notebooks or raw SQL. Sergey explicitly rejected that.
  2. Knowledge base that learns. BayOne's pipeline stores approved patterns for
  future runs. Generic products start fresh every time.
  3. Human-in-the-loop with surgical auto-fix. Not a black-box "run and pray"
  migration.
  4. "Solution, not product." This is Colin's framing from day one, and it lands

● Found the root cause. Since Mermaid v9.2, it uses foreignObject with HTML divs
   for labels, and the foreignObject elements are sized smaller than the text
  they contain. The fix is htmlLabels: false which forces SVG text rendering
  where box sizing actually works correctly.

● Web Search("mermaid.js htmlLabels false foreignObject fix text clipping
            flowchart node size")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

  htmlLabels: false, I cannot use <b> HTML tags in labels. I need to use
  Mermaid's native markdown syntax instead. Let me also check what that looks
  like.

● Web Search("mermaid.js markdown labels bold text "` `" backtick flowchart node

● Now I have the complete picture. The fix:
  1. htmlLabels: false to use SVG text (fixes clipping)
  2. useMaxWidth: false to prevent scaling issues
  3. Use Mermaid markdown strings with "` text `" syntax for bold (**text**) and
   line breaks (actual newlines)
  4. No HTML tags in labels

● Agent "Screenshot architecture diagram" completed
  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ But if HTML labels was true, is there a better way to do it? I don't really   
understand why we need to use SVG text.                                         

● You're right to question that. SVG text is a workaround, not a real fix. The
  actual problem with htmlLabels: true is that Mermaid's foreignObject elements
  get a fixed width/height calculated before the CSS font loads. So the box is
  sized for the fallback font, then Inter loads and the text is wider, and it
  clips.

  The real fix with htmlLabels: true (which is better because it supports <b>,
  <br/>, and proper formatting):

  1. Preload the font so it is available BEFORE Mermaid renders
  2. Delay Mermaid render until after fonts are loaded using
  document.fonts.ready
  3. Set useMaxWidth: false so Mermaid does not auto-shrink the SVG

  Let me look at the screenshot first to see the actual damage, then fix it
  properly.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

   portrait. Let me fix this properly with the font-preload approach.

● Done. Here is what changed and why:

  1. htmlLabels: false - Forces Mermaid to use native SVG <text> elements
  instead of foreignObject with HTML divs. SVG text elements measure correctly
  and boxes resize to fit. This is the documented fix for the clipping problem.
  2. useMaxWidth: false - Prevents Mermaid from auto-shrinking the diagram to
  fit the container width. The diagram renders at its natural size and scrolls
  horizontally if needed.
  3. Markdown string syntax - All node labels now use "`  **Bold Title**\nSecond
   line`" format instead of <b> and <br/> HTML tags. This is how Mermaid handles
   bold and multi-line text when htmlLabels is false.
  4. Removed all the foreignObject CSS hacks - No more overflow: visible,
  white-space: nowrap, document.fonts.ready, or post-render resize scripts.
  Those were bandaids for the wrong approach.
  5. All colors, styles, subgraph groupings, PostgreSQL placement, and page 
  layout remain the same as the version you said had good color coding.

  Please refresh and let me know how it looks.

✻ Worked for 2m 4s

❯ Okay, how do we add more padding around those label boxes and also have them  
as a solid background? Sometimes they overlap with some of the arrow lines, and 
 it would be better to show them as labels with a solid background than it      
would be to show it with the arrow running through the text.                    

● The Mermaid theme config has an edgeLabelBackground property that controls the
   fill, which we already set to #ede9fe. For a solid background that fully
  covers the arrow line behind it, I would:

  1. Increase padding by adding CSS to the edge label text elements: padding: 
  4px 10px on the SVG text or its container
  2. Ensure the rect fully covers the arrow by making the rect slightly larger
  via CSS stroke-width and ensuring no transparency in the fill

  However, with htmlLabels: false (SVG text mode), the edge label rects are
  rendered as SVG <rect> elements and the padding is controlled internally by
  Mermaid based on text measurement. The CSS override on the rect fill and
  stroke already works. To add more padding, I can try adding a CSS transform to
   scale the rect slightly larger than the text, or I can add extra spaces
  inside the edge label strings themselves in the Mermaid definition (e.g., |" 
  Deploy configs ")| with spaces padding the text).

  The spaces-in-label approach is the most reliable because it forces Mermaid to
   measure a wider string and draw a larger rect. The CSS approach for SVG rect
  sizing is less predictable.

  My recommendation: add padding spaces to each edge label string in both
  diagrams. For example:

  - |"Exported XML"| becomes |"  Exported XML  "|
  - |"Deploy configs"| becomes |"  Deploy configs  "|
  - etc.

  The solid background is already handled by the fill: #ede9fe !important CSS.
  As long as the rect is large enough (which the padding spaces ensure), it will
   fully cover any arrow line behind it.

  Shall I go ahead with adding the padding spaces to all edge labels?

✻ Cogitated for 5m 21s

❯ One thing that we are missing that you will need to get from exploring the    
codebase itself is what each of the gates does (G1, G2, etc) and what each      
agent does. That is what we are missing in this doc.                            

● I already have that information from the codebase analysis. Here is what I
  would add, and where:

  In Section 03 (Agent Pipeline Architecture), after the Mermaid diagram and
  before the "Design Principle" highlight box, I would add two tables:

  Table 1: Quality Gates

  Gate: G1
  Name: Orchestrator Gate
  What It Checks: All source artifacts loaded, DataStage XML present, target
    examples loaded, all artifacts have content, run ID generated
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Gate: G2
  Name: Parser Gate
  What It Checks: DataStage parser returned stages and embedded SQL, SQL
    interpreter produced results, DDL schemas parsed, column names grounded in
    source files, cross-check deterministic vs LLM table extraction
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Gate: G3
  Name: Mapper Gate
  What It Checks: Pattern mapping is non-empty, mapping references actual source

    table names from DDL schemas, mentions source references, type mappings, and

    column mappings
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Gate: G4
  Name: SQL Gate
  What It Checks: SQL is substantial (5000+ chars), sqlglot syntax check (50%+
    statements parse), DDL table coverage (30%+), column coverage (20%+), source

    table grounding (FROM/JOIN refs exist in source), truncation detection
    (end-of-file and per-view), HQL column match. Then LLM check: business logic

    preservation and column existence against Scala source
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Gate: G5
  Name: Config Gate
  What It Checks: Pipeline YAML valid and substantial (200+ chars), deployment
    YAML valid and substantial (100+ chars), HQL has CREATE TABLE, HQL columns
    grounded in target, YAML sourceFile names grounded in source. Then LLM
  check:
     token name matching, column type consistency vs SQL CASTs, deployment
  config
     structure

  Table 2: Agent Roles

  Agent: Orchestrator
  Model: Sonnet
  What It Does: Loads all source files, classifies each by type (DataStage XML,
    stored procedure, DDL, view, schema, Scala app, YAML, HQL), identifies which

    pipeline to build from target examples, generates run ID
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: DataStage Parser
  Model: Opus
  What It Does: Parses DataStage XML: extracts job stages, transformations,
    embedded SQL, column definitions using Python/sqlglot deterministically,
  then
     one Opus call to synthesize into structured analysis
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: SQL Interpreter
  Model: Sonnet
  What It Does: Analyzes stored procedures and views: extracts tables, joins,
    CTEs, temp tables via sqlglot, then parallel Sonnet batch calls for business

    rule extraction (flag calculations, aggregation patterns, temporal logic)
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: DDL Parser
  Model: Sonnet
  What It Does: Parses DDL files and views: extracts table names, column names
    with exact decimal precision, nullable constraints, primary keys via
  sqlglot,
     then parallel Sonnet batch calls for semantic analysis
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: Pattern Mapper
  Model: Opus
  What It Does: Single Opus call. Reads all parser outputs plus target
  Scala/YAML
    examples. Produces translation dictionary: surrogate keys to business keys,
    SQL Server types to Databricks types, temp tables to intermediate views,
  CASE
     WHEN patterns, GETDATE to current_date
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: Spark SQL Generator
  Model: Opus + Sonnet
  What It Does: Three-phase: (1) Opus plans all stages and builds dependency
    graph of independent vs dependent stages, (2) Sonnet generates independent
    stages in parallel, (3) Opus generates dependent stages with Phase 1 output
    as context. On retry: single Opus call with previous SQL plus errors for
    targeted fix
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: Config Generator
  Model: 3x Sonnet
  What It Does: Three parallel Sonnet calls, one per file: pipeline YAML,
    deployment YAML, create.HQL. Each copies the target template structure
    exactly, only changing values where the generated Spark SQL requires it
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: Schema Validator
  Model: None (deterministic)
  What It Does: Zero LLM calls. Cross-references all generated outputs against
    each other and against source artifacts. Assembles gate LLM findings from
    upstream. Computes overall score. Produces the validation result for the
    review screen
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Agent: Human Approval
  Model: None
  What It Does: LangGraph interrupt for human review. Presents validation score
    and issues. Approve proceeds to END. Reject routes back to Spark SQL
    Generator with error context. Auto-approve after configurable threshold

  Shall I go ahead and add these two tables to Section 03 of the combined
  document?
